class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="above" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-size:130%; color: black; in Ireland (European Commission 2012)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;"><span background-color:  #c9ffd9;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<i>None</i></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-top:0.225em;line-height:1.1em; padding-right:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/IETF_language_tag" title="IETF language tag">IETF</a></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<code>en-IE</code></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Hiberno\xe2\x80\x90English</b> (from <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Hibernia" title="Hibernia">Hibernia</a></i>: "Ireland") or <b>Irish English</b><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> is the set of English <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> natively written and spoken within the island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> (including both the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>English was brought to Ireland as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Norman_invasion_of_Ireland" title="Norman invasion of Ireland">Norman invasion of Ireland</a> of the late 12th century. Initially, it was mainly spoken in an area known as <a href="/wiki/The_Pale" title="The Pale">the Pale</a> around <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, with mostly <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> spoken throughout the rest of the country. By the <a href="/wiki/Tudor_period" title="Tudor period">Tudor period</a>, Irish culture and language had regained most of the territory lost to the invaders: even in the Pale, "all the common folk\xe2\x80\xa6 for the most part are of Irish birth, Irish habit, and of Irish language".<sup id="cite_ref-multitext.ucc.ie_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-multitext.ucc.ie-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Some small pockets remained predominantly English-speaking; because of their sheer isolation their dialects developed into later (now extinct) dialects known as <a href="/wiki/Forth_and_Bargy_dialect" title="Forth and Bargy dialect">Yola</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_Wexford" title="County Wexford">Wexford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fingallian" title="Fingallian">Fingallian</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fingal" title="Fingal">Fingal</a>, Dublin. These were no longer mutually intelligible with other English varieties. However, <a href="/wiki/Tudor_conquest_of_Ireland" title="Tudor conquest of Ireland">the Tudor conquest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plantations_of_Ireland" title="Plantations of Ireland">colonisation</a> of Ireland in the 16th century marked a revival in the use of English. By the mid-19th century, English was the majority language spoken in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup>  It has retained this status to the present day, with even those whose first language is Irish being fluent in English as well. Today, there is only a little more than one percent of the population that speaks Irish natively.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> English is one of two official languages, along with Irish, of the Republic of Ireland, and is the country\'s <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">de facto</i> working language.\n</p><p>Hiberno-English\'s <a href="/wiki/American_and_British_English_spelling_differences" title="American and British English spelling differences">spelling</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_and_British_English_pronunciation_differences" title="American and British English pronunciation differences">pronunciation standards</a> align with British rather than American English. However, Hiberno-English\'s diverse accents and some of its grammatical structures are unique, with some influence by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> and a tendency to be <a href="/wiki/Phonology" title="Phonology">phonologically</a> <a href="/wiki/Conservative_(linguistics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative (linguistics)">conservative</a>, retaining older features no longer common in the accents of England or North America.\n</p><p>Phonologists today often divide Hiberno-English into four or five overarching classes of <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> or accents:<sup id="cite_ref-de_Gruyter_2004_90\xe2\x80\x9393_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Gruyter_2004_90\xe2\x80\x9393-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ulster_English" title="Ulster English">Ulster accents</a>, West and South-West Region accents (including, for example, the Cork accent), various Dublin accents, and a supraregional accent developing since only the last quarter of the twentieth century.\n</p>\n<div class="toclimit-4"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ulster_English">Ulster English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ulster English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Ulster_English" title="Ulster English">Ulster English</a> (or <b>Northern Irish English</b>) here refers collectively to the varieties of the <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a> province, including <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> and neighbouring counties outside of Northern Ireland, which has been influenced by <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Irish" title="Ulster Irish">Ulster Irish</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots language</a>, brought over by Scottish settlers during the <a href="/wiki/Plantation_of_Ulster" title="Plantation of Ulster">Plantation of Ulster</a>. Its main subdivisions are <b>Mid-Ulster English</b> , <b>South Ulster English</b> and <b><a href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots_dialects" title="Ulster Scots dialects">Ulster Scots English</a></b>, the latter of which is more directly and strongly influenced by the Scots language. All Ulster English has more obvious pronunciation similarities with <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">Scottish English</a> than other Irish English dialects do.\n</p><p>Ulster varieties distinctly pronounce:\n</p>\n<ul><li>An ordinarily grammatically structured (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Topicalization" title="Topicalization">non-topicalised</a>) <a href="/wiki/Declarative_sentence" class="mw-redirect" title="Declarative sentence">declarative sentences</a>, often, with a <a href="/wiki/High_rising_terminal" title="High rising terminal">rising intonation at the end</a> of the sentence (the type of intonation pattern that other English speakers usually associate with <a href="/wiki/Question" title="Question">questions</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as lowered, in the general vicinity of <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc3\xab~\xc9\x98~\xc9\xaa\xcc\x88]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xca\x8c/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">\xca\x8c</span></span>/</a></span></span> as fronted and slightly rounded, more closely approaching <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x9e]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/u\xcb\x90/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">u\xcb\x90</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xca\x8a/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;push&#39;">\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> both in the general vicinity of <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xca\x89]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> with a backed on-glide and fronted off-glide, putting it in the vicinity of <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x90\xca\x8f~\xc9\x9c\xca\x89]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x9b\xc9\xaa~\xc9\x9c\xc9\xaa]</a></span>, particularly before <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless consonant">voiceless consonants</a>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[e\xcb\x90]</a></span>, though nowadays commonly <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[e\xcb\x90\xc9\x99]</a></span> or even <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\xaa\xcb\x90\xc9\x99]</a></span> when in a <a href="/wiki/Closed_syllable" class="mw-redirect" title="Closed syllable">closed syllable</a>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span>, almost always, as a slightly raised <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthong</a> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[o\xcc\x9d(:)]</a></span>.</li>\n<li>A lack of <a href="/wiki/Happy-tensing" class="mw-redirect" title="Happy-tensing"><i>happy</i>-tensing</a>; with the final vowel of <i>happy, holy, money,</i> etc. as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[e]</a></span>.</li>\n<li>Syllable-final <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> occasionally as "<a href="/wiki/Velarized_alveolar_lateral_approximant" class="mw-redirect" title="Velarized alveolar lateral approximant">dark [\xc9\xab]</a>", though especially before a consonant.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_lifelong_native_speakers">Notable lifelong native speakers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Notable lifelong native speakers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Christine_Bleakley" class="mw-redirect" title="Christine Bleakley">Christine Bleakley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dornan" title="Jamie Dornan">Jamie Dornan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rory_McIlroy" title="Rory McIlroy">Rory McIlroy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "The Northern Irish accent is the sexiest in the UK, according to a new poll. The dulcet tones of Liam Neeson, Jamie Dornan, Christine Bleakley and Rory McIlroy helped ensure the accent came top of the popularity charts"<sup id="cite_ref-sexy_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexy-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/John_Cole_(journalist)" title="John Cole (journalist)">John Cole</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "His distinctive Ulster accent"<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nadine_Coyle" title="Nadine Coyle">Nadine Coyle</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "I was born and raised in Derry and I can\'t change the way I talk".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_O%27Donnell" title="Daniel O&#39;Donnell">Daniel O\'Donnell</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "the languid Donegal accent made famous by Daniel O\'Donnell"<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Colin_Morgan" title="Colin Morgan">Colin Morgan</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "Colin Morgan has revealed that fans of the show are often confused by his accent. The 23-year-old... is originally from Northern Ireland"<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="West_and_South-West_Irish_English">West and South-West Irish English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: West and South-West Irish English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><b>West and South-West Irish English</b> here refers to <a href="/wiki/Broad_and_general_accents" title="Broad and general accents">broad varieties</a> of Ireland\'s <a href="/wiki/West_Region,_Ireland" title="West Region, Ireland">West</a> and <a href="/wiki/South-West_Region,_Ireland" title="South-West Region, Ireland">South-West</a> Regions. Accents of both regions are known for:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Pin%E2%80%93pen_merger" class="mw-redirect" title="Pin\xe2\x80\x93pen merger">pin\xe2\x80\x93pen merger</a><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The backing and slight lowering of <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> towards <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x90\xca\x8a~\xca\x8c\xca\x8a]</a></span>.</li>\n<li>The more open starting point for <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90</span></span>/</a></span></span> of <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x91\xcb\x90\xc9\xb9~\xc3\xa4\xcb\x90\xc9\xb9]</a></span> and <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x91\xcb\x90~\xc3\xa4]</a></span>, respectively.</li>\n<li>The preservation of <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthongal</a> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[o\xcb\x90]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xce\xb8/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thigh&#39;">\xce\xb8</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc3\xb0/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thy&#39;">\xc3\xb0</span></span>/</a></span></span>, respectively, as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[t~t\xca\xb0]</a></span> and <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[d]</a></span>.</li>\n<li>In the West, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>/</a></span></span> may respectively be pronounced as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x83/</span> and <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x92/</span> before a consonant, so <i>fist</i> sounds like <i>fisht</i>, <i>castle</i> like <i>cashle</i>, and <i>arrest</i> like <i>arresht</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>South-West Irish English</b> (often known, by specific <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Ireland" title="Counties of Ireland">county</a>, as <b>Cork English</b>, <b>Kerry English</b>, or <b>Limerick English</b>) also features two major defining characteristics of its own: the raising of <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x9b/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">\xc9\x9b</span></span>/</a></span></span> to [\xc9\xaa] when before /n/ or /m/ (as in <i>again</i> or <i>pen</i>), and the noticeable intonation pattern of a slightly higher pitch followed by a significant drop in pitch on stressed long-vowel syllables (across multiple syllables or even within a single one),<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> which is popularly heard, in rapid conversation, as a kind of undulating "sing-song" pattern.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_lifelong_native_speakers_2">Notable lifelong native speakers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Notable lifelong native speakers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Roy_Keane" title="Roy Keane">Roy Keane</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "Cork accent"<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1ith%C3%AD_%C3%93_S%C3%A9" title="D\xc3\xa1ith\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 S\xc3\xa9">D\xc3\xa1ith\xc3\xad \xc3\x93 S\xc3\xa9</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "his Kerry dialect"<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Rubberbandits" title="The Rubberbandits">The Rubberbandits</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "Rubberbandits\' strong Limerick accent... sits on a frequency like a tambourine which can cut through any noise"<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dublin_English">Dublin English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Dublin English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><b>Dublin English</b> is highly internally diverse and refers collectively to the Irish English varieties immediately surrounding and within the metropolitan area of <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. Modern-day Dublin English largely lies on a <a href="/wiki/Phonology" title="Phonology">phonological</a> continuum,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This appears obvious to my experience, though a source that digs deeper into this would be great (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> ranging from a more traditional, lower-prestige, local urban accent on the one end to a more recently developing, higher-prestige, non-local (regional and even supraregional) accent on the other end, whose most advanced characteristics only first emerged in the late 1980s and 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Dartspeak_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dartspeak-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The accent that most strongly uses the traditional working-class features has been labelled by linguistis as <b>local Dublin English</b>. Most speakers from Dublin and its suburbs, however, have accent features falling variously along the entire middle as well as newer end of the spectrum, which together form what is called <b>non-local Dublin English</b>, spoken by middle- and upper-class natives of Dublin and the greater eastern Irish region surrounding the city. A subset of this variety, whose middle-class speakers mostly range in the middle section of the continuum, is called <b>mainstream Dublin English</b>. Mainstream Dublin English has become the basis of an accent that has otherwise become supraregional (see more below) everywhere except in the north of the country. The majority of Dubliners born since the 1980s (led particularly by females) has shifted towards the most innovative non-local accent, here called <b>new Dublin English</b>, which has gained ground over mainstream Dublin English and which is the most extreme variety in rejecting the local accent\'s traditional features.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The varieties at either extreme of the spectrum, local and new Dublin English, are both discussed in further detail below. In the most general terms, all varieties of Dublin English have the following identifying sounds that are often distinct from the rest of Ireland, pronouncing:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as fronted and/or raised <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc3\xa6\xca\x8a~\xc9\x9b\xca\x8a~e\xca\x8a]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as retracted and/or centralised <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x99\xc9\xaa~\xc9\x91\xc9\xaa]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as a <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a> in the range (local to non-local) of <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xca\x8c\xca\x8a~o\xca\x8a~\xc9\x99\xca\x8a]</a></span>.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_Dublin_English">Local Dublin English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Local Dublin English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>Local Dublin English</b> (or <b>popular Dublin English</b>) here refers to a traditional, <a href="/wiki/Broad_and_general_accents" title="Broad and general accents">broad</a>, working-class variety spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>\'s capital city of <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. It is the only Irish English variety that in earlier history was non-rhotic; however, it is today weakly rhotic,<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-de_Gruyter_2004_91_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Gruyter_2004_91-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and it uniquely pronounces:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x99\xc9\xaa]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x9b\xca\x8a~e\xca\x8a]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa/: &#39;oi&#39; in &#39;choice&#39;">\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[a\xc9\xaa~\xc3\xa4\xc9\xaa]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xca\x8c\xca\x8a~\xca\x8co]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xca\x8c/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">\xca\x8c</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xca\x8a]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xce\xb8/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thigh&#39;">\xce\xb8</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc3\xb0/: &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thy&#39;">\xc3\xb0</span></span>/</a></span></span>, respectively, as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[t(\xca\xb0)]</a></span> and <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[d]</a></span>.</li></ul>\n<p>The local Dublin accent is also known for a phenomenon called "vowel breaking", in which the vowel sounds <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/u\xcb\x90/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">u\xcb\x90</span></span>/</a></span></span>, and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/i\xcb\x90/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">i\xcb\x90</span></span>/</a></span></span> in <a href="/wiki/Closed_syllable" class="mw-redirect" title="Closed syllable">closed syllables</a> are "broken" into two syllables, approximating <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x9bw\xc9\x99]</a></span>, <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x99j\xc9\x99]</a></span>, <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[uw\xc9\x99]</a></span>, and <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ij\xc9\x99]</a></span>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_lifelong_native_speakers_3">Notable lifelong native speakers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Notable lifelong native speakers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Damien_Dempsey" title="Damien Dempsey">Damien Dempsey</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "his distinctly Dublin sounds" and "a working class Dublin accent"<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Imelda_May" title="Imelda May">Imelda May</a>  \xe2\x80\x93 "Irish celebrities who have distinctive accents \xe2\x80\x94 such as Imelda May"<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Conor_McGregor" title="Conor McGregor">Conor McGregor</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Dublin_English">New Dublin English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: New Dublin English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Evolving as a fashionable outgrowth of the mainstream non-local Dublin English, <b>new Dublin English</b> (also, <b>advanced Dublin English</b> and, formerly, <b>fashionable Dublin English</b>) is a youthful variety that originally began in the early 1990s among the "<a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a>" and now those aspiring to a non-local "urban sophistication".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> New Dublin English itself, first associated with affluent and middle-class inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Southside_Dublin" class="mw-redirect" title="Southside Dublin">southside Dublin</a>, is probably now spoken by a majority of Dubliners born since the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-Dartspeak_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dartspeak-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> It has replaced (yet was largely influenced by) moribund <b><a href="/wiki/Dublin_4" title="Dublin 4">D4</a> English</b> (often known as "Dublin 4" or "<a href="/wiki/Dublin_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Dublin Area Rapid Transit">DART</a> speak" or, mockingly, "Dortspeak"), which originated around the 1970s from Dubliners who rejected traditional notions of Irishness, regarding themselves as more trendy and sophisticated;<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> however, particular aspects of the D4 accent became quickly noticed and ridiculed as sounding affected, causing these features to fall out of fashion by the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Dublin_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dublin-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This "new mainstream" accent of Dublin\'s youth, rejecting traditional working-class Dublin, pronounces:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span></span>/</a></span></span> as open as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[a]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;far&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90r</span></span>/</a></span></span> may be <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc3\xa4\xcb\x90\xc9\xb9]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-r.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/En-us-r.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-r.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, with a backer vowel than in other Irish accents, though still relatively fronted.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90</span></span>/</a></span></span> as high as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x94\xcb\x90]</a></span> or even <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[o\xcb\x90]</a></span>, causing a re-split in the <a href="/wiki/Cot%E2%80%93caught_merger" title="Cot\xe2\x80\x93caught merger">cot\xe2\x80\x93caught merger</a> that traditionally characterised Dublin speech.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa/: &#39;oi&#39; in &#39;choice&#39;">\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as high as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa]</a></span> or even <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[o\xc9\xaa]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as the Londonian <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x99\xca\x8a]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-oh.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/En-uk-oh.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-oh.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r/: &#39;are&#39; in &#39;bare&#39;">\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r</span></span>/</a></span></span> as both possibly rounded <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc3\xb8\xcb\x90\xc9\xbb]</a></span>, perhaps causing a <a href="/wiki/English-language_vowel_changes_before_historic_/r/#Square\xe2\x80\x93nurse_merger" title="English-language vowel changes before historic /r/">fur\xe2\x80\x93fair merger</a>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span></span>/</a></span></span> as possibly merged, as well as <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;w&#39; in &#39;wind&#39;">w</span></span>/</a></span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/hw/: &#39;wh&#39; in &#39;why&#39;">hw</span></span>/</a></span></span> as possibly merged, leading to potential <a href="/wiki/Horse%E2%80%93hoarse_merger" class="mw-redirect" title="Horse\xe2\x80\x93hoarse merger">horse\xe2\x80\x93hoarse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Witch%E2%80%93which_merger" class="mw-redirect" title="Witch\xe2\x80\x93which merger">witch\xe2\x80\x93which mergers</a>.</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_lifelong_native_speakers_4">Notable lifelong native speakers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Notable lifelong native speakers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Saoirse_Ronan" title="Saoirse Ronan">Saoirse Ronan</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "the \'Dub\' accent in which she speaks"<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Scott_(actor)" title="Andrew Scott (actor)">Andrew Scott</a> \xe2\x80\x93 "his soft-as-rain Dublin accent"<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supraregional_southern_Irish_English">Supraregional southern Irish English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Supraregional southern Irish English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><b>Supraregional southern Irish English</b> (sometimes, simply, <b>supraregional Irish English</b> or <b>supraregional Hiberno-English</b>) here refers to a variety crossing regional boundaries throughout all of the Republic of Ireland, except the north. As mentioned earlier, <b>mainstream Dublin English</b> of the early- to mid-1900s is the direct influence and catalyst for this variety.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Most speakers born in the 1980s or later are showing fewer features of the twentieth-century mainstream supraregional form and more characteristics of an advanced supraregional variety that aligns clearly with the rapidly spreading new Dublin accent (see more above, under "Non-local Dublin English").<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ireland\'s supraregional dialect pronounces:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc3\xa6/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">\xc3\xa6</span></span>/</a></span></span> as quite open <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[a]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> along a possible spectrum <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[a\xc9\xaa~\xc3\xa4\xc9\xaa~\xc9\x91\xc9\xaa]</a></span>, with innovative [\xc9\x91\xc9\xaa] particularly more common before <a href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced consonant">voiced consonants</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-de_Gruyter_2004_91_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Gruyter_2004_91-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> notably including /r/.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as starting fronter and often more raised than other dialects: <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[a\xca\x8a~\xc3\xa6\xca\x8a~\xc9\x9b\xca\x8a]</span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;far&#39;">\xc9\x91\xcb\x90r</span></span>/</a></span></span> may be <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc3\xa4\xcb\x90\xc9\xb9]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-r.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/En-us-r.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-r.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, with a backer vowel than in other Irish accents, though still relatively fronted.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x92\xcb\x90]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x92\xcb\x90\xc9\xb9]</a></span>, almost always separate from <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[o\xcb\x90\xc9\xb9]</a></span>, keeping words like <i>war</i> and <i>wore</i>, or <i>horse</i> and <i>hoarse</i>, pronounced distinctly.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa/: &#39;oi&#39; in &#39;choice&#39;">\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span> as <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x92\xc9\xaa]</a></span>.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span> as a <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a>, approaching <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[o\xca\x8a]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-o.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7d/En-us-o.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-o.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, as in the mainstream United States, or <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[\xc9\x99\xca\x8a]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-oh.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b1/En-uk-oh.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-oh.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>, as in mainstream England.</li>\n<li><span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xca\x8c/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">\xca\x8c</span></span>/</a></span></span> as higher, fronter, and often rounder <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc9\x99~\xca\x8a]</span>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_of_pronunciation_and_phonology">Overview of pronunciation and phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Overview of pronunciation and phonology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following charts list the vowels typical of each Irish English dialect as well as the several distinctive consonants of Irish English.<sup id="cite_ref-de_Gruyter_2004_90\xe2\x80\x9393_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Gruyter_2004_90\xe2\x80\x9393-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Phonological characteristics of overall Irish English are given as well as categorisations into five major divisions of Hiberno-English: northern Ireland (or Ulster); West &amp; South-West Ireland; local Dublin; new Dublin; and supraregional (southern) Ireland. Features of mainstream non-local Dublin English fall on a range between "local Dublin" and "new Dublin".\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Pure_vowels_.28monophthongs.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pure_vowels_(monophthongs)">Pure vowels (monophthongs)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pure vowels (monophthongs)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>The defining <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthongs</a> of Irish English:</b>\n</p><p>The following pure vowel sounds are defining characteristics of Irish English:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The vowel <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xca\x8c/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">\xca\x8c</span></span>/</a></span></span>, as in <i>cut</i> or <i>run</i>, is typically <a href="/wiki/Central_vowel" title="Central vowel">centralised</a> in the mouth and often somewhat more rounded than other standard English varieties, such as <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">Received Pronunciation</a> in England or <a href="/wiki/General_American" title="General American">General American</a> in the United States.</li>\n<li>Most Irish English varieties make some distinction between the <a href="/wiki/Trap-bath_split" title="Trap-bath split">"broad" <i>a</i> and "flat" <i>a</i></a> of Received Pronunciation, whereas <a href="/wiki/General_American" title="General American">General American</a>, for example, makes no distinction.</li>\n<li>There is inconsistency regarding the <a href="/wiki/Lot%E2%80%93cloth_split" class="mw-redirect" title="Lot\xe2\x80\x93cloth split">lot\xe2\x80\x93cloth split</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cot%E2%80%93caught_merger" title="Cot\xe2\x80\x93caught merger">cot\xe2\x80\x93caught merger</a>; certain Irish English dialects have these phenomena while others do not.</li>\n<li><i>Any</i> and <i>many</i> are pronounced to rhyme with <i>nanny</i>, <i>Danny</i>, etc. by very many speakers, i.e. with each of these words pronounced with <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[\xc3\xa6]</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>All pure vowels of various Hiberno-English dialects:</b>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" />Dublin</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>Supraregional <br />Ireland</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>Example words</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Trap-bath_split" title="Trap-bath split">flat</a> <span l<b>o</b>ss, <b>o</b>ff\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" <b>a</b>ren<b>a</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\xaa/</span><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" t<b>i</b>p\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i\xcb\x90/</span><sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_happy"><a href="#endnote_happy">4</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td colspan="5">[i(\xcb\x90)]<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_vowelbreak"><a fl<b>oo</b>d, wh<b>a</b>t\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x8a/</span>\n</td>\n<td>[\xca\x89]\n</td>\n<td href="#endnote_vowelbreak">3</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>[u\xcb\x90]\n</td>\n<td>f<b>oo</b>d, gl<b>ue</b>, n<b>ew</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Footnotes:</b>\n</p><p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_D4"><b><a href="#ref_D4">^1</a></b></span> \nIn <a href="/wiki/Southside_Dublin" class="mw-redirect" title="Southside Dublin">southside Dublin</a>\'s once-briefly fashionable "<a href="/wiki/Dublin_4" title="Dublin 4">Dublin 4</a>" (or "Dortspeak") accent, the "<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/</span> and broad <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc3\xa6/</span>" set becomes rounded as [\xc9\x92\xcb\x90].<sup id="cite_ref-Dublin_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dublin-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_SW"><b><a href="#ref_SW">^2</a></b></span>  In South-West Ireland, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x9b/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">\xc9\x9b</span></span>/</a></span></span> before /n/ or /m/ is raised to [\xc9\xaa].<sup id="cite_ref-South-West_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South-West-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_vowelbreak"><b><a href="#ref_vowelbreak">^3</a></b></span>  Due to the local Dublin accent\'s phenomenon of "vowel breaking", /i\xcb\x90/ may be realised in this accent as [ij\xc9\x99] in a <a href="/wiki/Closed_syllable" class="mw-redirect" title="Closed syllable">closed syllable</a>, and, in the same environment, /u\xcb\x90/ may be realised as [\xca\x8auw\xc9\x99].\n</p><p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_happy"><b><a href="#ref_happy">^4</a></b></span> Unstressed syllable-final /i\xcb\x90/ or /\xc9\xaa/ is realised in Ulster accents uniquely as [e~\xc9\xaa].<sup id="cite_ref-de_Gruyter_2004_91_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-de_Gruyter_2004_91-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Other notes:</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>In some highly conservative Irish English varieties, words spelled with <i>ea</i> and pronounced with <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[i\xcb\x90]</span> in RP are pronounced with <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[e\xcb\x90]</span>, for example <i>meat</i>, <i>beat</i>, and <i>leaf</i>.</li>\n<li>In words like <i>took</i> where the spelling "oo" usually represents <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xca\x8a/</span>, conservative speakers may use <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/u\xcb\x90/</span>. This is most common in local Dublin and the speech of north-east Leinster.</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Gliding_vowels_.28diphthongs.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gliding_vowels_(diphthongs)">Gliding vowels (diphthongs)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hiberno-English&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Gliding vowels (diphthongs)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>The defining <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongs</a> of Hiberno-English:</b>\n</p><p>The following gliding vowel (diphthong) sounds are defining characteristics of Irish English:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The first element of the diphthong <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span>, as in <i>ow</i> or <i>doubt</i>, may move forward in the mouth in the east (namely, Dublin) and supraregionally; however, it may actually move backward throughout the entire rest of the country. In the north alone, the second element is particularly moved forward, as in Scotland.</li>\n<li>The first element of the diphthong <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa/: &#39;oi&#39; in &#39;choice&#39;">\xc9\x94\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span>, as in <i>boy</i> or <i>choice</i>, is slightly or significantly lowered in all geographic regions except the north.</li>\n<li>The diphthong <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">e\xc9\xaa</span></span>/</a></span></span>, as in <i>rain</i> or <i>bay</i>, is most commonly <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthongised</a> to <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[e\xcb\x90]</a></span>. Furthermore, this often lowers to <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/\xc9\x9b/</span> in words such as <i>gave</i> and <i>came</i> (sounding like "gev" and "kem").<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>All diphthongs of various Hiberno-English dialects:</b>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n<caption>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td><b>English <br />diaphoneme</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>Ulster</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>West &amp; <br />South-West Ireland</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>Local <br />Dublin</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>New<br />Dublin</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>Supraregional <br />Ireland</b>\n</td>\n<td><b>Example words</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_vowelbreak"><a href="#endnote_vowelbreak">1</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>[a\xca\x8a~\xc9\x9b\xca\x8a]\n</td>\n<td>n<b>ow</b>, <b>ou</b>ch, sc<b>ou</b>t\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"
